        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1601695292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17345264090556199469"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>THE RAVEN PRINCE was the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/187063-unapologetic-romance-readers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unapologetic Romance Readers</a>' December book of the month pick, and I <i>barely </i>scraped by, finishing the book on December 29th. But I <i>did </i>scrape by, and am proud of it! I was initially excited that RAVEN PRINCE had run, because I really liked the other book I'd read in this trilogy, THE LEOPARD PRINCE, and this one was supposed to be even better.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Here's the thing about Elizabeth Hoyt - she's really hit and miss. When</span>
  <span id="freeText17345264090556199469" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>THE RAVEN PRINCE was the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/187063-unapologetic-romance-readers" rel="nofollow noopener">Unapologetic Romance Readers</a>' December book of the month pick, and I <i>barely </i>scraped by, finishing the book on December 29th. But I <i>did </i>scrape by, and am proud of it! I was initially excited that RAVEN PRINCE had run, because I really liked the other book I'd read in this trilogy, THE LEOPARD PRINCE, and this one was supposed to be even better.<br><br><br><br>Here's the thing about Elizabeth Hoyt - she's really hit and miss. When she's on her game, she hits balls out of the court left and right. She's written one of my favorite historical romances of all time (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1601088306" rel="nofollow noopener">DUKE OF SIN</a>). But man, when she's not on her game, the results are - in keeping with the sports metaphors - <i>foul</i>.<br><br><br><br>THE RAVEN PRINCE isn't a bad book. Most of the members in our buddy read really liked the book, and I did, too. But it isn't a prime example of Hoyt's works by any means and suffers from some major problems which I'm going to discuss.<br><br><br><br>***WARNING: MILD SPOILERS***<br><br><br><br>The plot is pretty simple. Anna Wren is a widow who is living in poverty with her mother-in-law, Mother Wren, and a loyal servant named Fanny. They're running out of money and on the cusp of making the terrible decision that no lady should make: starve in dignity like a lady or work like one of the peons? *rolls eyes* Luckily, Anna is able to secure a prestigious position as the local Earl's secretary, and he is none the wiser at first because she's hired by his man while he's on a trip. When he gets back, he admires her work before he learns of her sex (again, very luckily), and he decides to keep her on as a lark, and because she makes his naughty bits feel funny.<br><br><br><br>There's a bit of a Beauty and the Beast element to this book, because the Earl is terribly scarred all over because of small pox. I was wondering why this sounded so familiar, and then it occurred to me that I had read a book with the same trope earlier this month: Tessa Dare's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993015311" rel="nofollow noopener">THE DUCHESS DEAL</a>, except in the case of the duke in that story, the result of the scarring was fire from explosives. Anna is attracted to the Earl but her late husband cheated on her, so she doesn't want to jump into anything with another man because she is so damaged emotionally. #notallmen<br><br><br><br>There's a side plot where Anna ends up making the acquaintance of two prostitutes named Cora and Pearl, and they end up owing an Anna a favor when she saves Pearl from dying in the road. Anna decides to go to this brothel named Aphrodite's Grotto because she knows that the Earl plans to go there and she wants to sleep with him incognito, by means of a mask. Cora makes arrangements and the Earl has THE BEST LOVINS EVAR ™, so he comes back several times, but Anna has second thoughts and ditches him on what is supposed to be the third night, bemoaning her virtue and her feelings. There's also another sideplot involving blackmail (and the woman who cheated with Anna's husband), and the Earl finds out who Anna is and offers her marriage (in anger, at first) - except he's engaged to another woman so first he has to call that off, and while he is, Anna is contacted by the blackmailer and runs away, and there's drama, but then everyone winds up happy, the end.<br><br>
  <br>
<br>There were several reasons I didn't like this book as much as I should have. I don't generally like stories where the characters have sex with each other not knowing who the other is. It feels icky. There was only one book that I didn't mind that trope in, and that was a bodice-ripper; I expect those kinds of shenanigans from bodice rippers. The way Anna reacted afterwards just felt so convoluted, too. She was very emotionally vulnerable, but that disappeared whenever it was convenient to the plot, so she came across as undeveloped. Same with the Earl. Sometimes you read about characters who feel fully fleshed out and human, and you feel invested with them. These characters felt like little puppets moving around on a stage. I didn't feel invested in them at all.<br><br>
  <br>
<br>Another trope this book employs that I don't like is the "I was barren until I ended up with the right man" trope. I tried to tell myself that maybe Anna wasn't barren, but her husband was - but then I remembered that her husband was cheating on her with another woman, and (it's <i>heavily implied</i>) got said OW with child. Of <i>course </i>Anna is only able to have children when she ends up with her true love. *rolls eyes* I don't know, something about this feels vaguely ableist, like it's sending the message to barren women, "Oh, you're just not trying hard enough" or "you're just not with the right person." It feels gross and manipulative, and I don't like this trope at all - but it's used a <i>lot</i>.<br><br>
  <br>
<br>I did like the fact that Anna wasn't another virginal widow (another trope I hate), and her relationship with her mother-in-law was genuinely touching. All the secondary characters in this book are also excellent, like Hopple and his bumblebee and frog waistcoats, the cranky and mutinous Davis, Cora and Pearl (of course), and Mother Wren. They actually stole the show from the main characters, which is a problem. But the writing is good, and the garden scenes (there were several) are so magical that they reminded me of the reveal in THE SECRET GARDEN, and there were some pretty steamy moments in THE RAVEN PRINCE, so I guess I can't fault it **too** much.<br><br>
  <br>
<br>3 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="17345264090556199469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117284007?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammy Walton Grant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammy Walton Grant" href="/user/show/3047961-tammy-walton-grant">Tammy Walton Grant</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/7707886-the-raven-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047961-tammy-walton-grant?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047961-tammy-walton-grant?shelf=2011-february">2011-february</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047961-tammy-walton-grant?shelf=tropes-beauty-and-the-beast">tropes-beauty-and-the-beast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047961-tammy-walton-grant?shelf=hr-oh-so-steamy">hr-oh-so-steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047961-tammy-walton-grant?shelf=hr-georgian">hr-georgian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047961-tammy-walton-grant?shelf=romance-series-not-so-much">romance-series-not-so-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047961-tammy-walton-grant?shelf=2011-april">2011-april</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047961-tammy-walton-grant?shelf=tropes-but-youre-my-boss">tropes-but-youre-my-boss</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117284007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17422726641047437235">4.5 stars<br/><br/>One of the problems with reading a very popular romance novel after everyone on the planet has already read it, is trying to find something to say about why you loved it that isn't the same as everyone else. Everyone has already talked about story, the depth, the meaning, the writing, the Beauty and the Beast angle, the main characters, the steamy scenes - what's left?<br/><br/>I loved this everything about this book. It's going on my favourites shelf - where I keep the books that I re-read and l</span>
  <span id="freeText17422726641047437235" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />One of the problems with reading a very popular romance novel after everyone on the planet has already read it, is trying to find something to say about why you loved it that isn't the same as everyone else. Everyone has already talked about story, the depth, the meaning, the writing, the Beauty and the Beast angle, the main characters, the steamy scenes - what's left?<br /><br />I loved this everything about this book. It's going on my favourites shelf - where I keep the books that I re-read and love most of all. There is something about it that enables me to lose myself in the story, feel the attraction, feel the tension between them, fall in love with Edward and wish I was Anna. One of my favourite scenes is one where Edward has bet Anna that she can't make his dog answer to a name she has just given it, and the forfeit is a kiss: <br /><br /><blockquote>Anna began to tremble. He bent his dark head toward hers, and his warm breath caressed her lips. She closed her eyes. And heard the dog clatter into the yard. Anna opened her eyes. Lord Swartingham was frozen. Slowly he turned his head, still only inches from hers, to stare at the canine. The dog grinned back, tongue hanging from his mouth, panting. "Shit," the earl breathed. <i>Quite</i>, Anna thought.</blockquote><br /><br />Part of the appeal for me is in the way that Edward and Anna are portrayed. Neither is "stop-traffic" gorgeous. It takes a second look before you appreciate the beauty of Edward's eyes, for example, or the shape of Anna's mouth. There is so much more depth to a person, imo, when their wit and their personality is part of what makes them attractive. This is what attracts me in real life and I suppose it follows me into my reading. Plastic, barbie-doll beauty has never held any appeal for me - either in men or women. (Unless it's Halle Barry. That woman is so beautiful she exists on a whole other plane.)<br /><br />Anyway. That's what I liked the most about this book. Elizabeth Hoyt forces you to look past the scars and the grumpiness to see the serious hottie hiding behind them. Oh all right, and the lonely man convinced no one will want him because of those scars. (That's the touchy-feely part. I just thought Edward was seriously sexy.)<br /><br />So no matter which romance trope is your favourite -- Ugly Duckling, widow/spinster, Beauty and the Beast, boss/secretary, this one has a bit of everything. Throw in some hilarious secondary characters (I'm thinking of Edward's valet, Davis), an intriguing fallen woman, and an excellent introduction to The Princes, Leopard and Serpent, and you end up with a book that was, for me, almost perfect.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1596453531" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1596453531" />
    <a title="Zoe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6168938-zoe"><img alt="Zoe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513974112p2/6168938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1596453531?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe" href="/user/show/6168938-zoe">Zoe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6130236-the-raven-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1596453531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16004491165576575121">OK I am going to say something that is very unpopular here: I did not like this book. <br/><br/>I believe that this book was Elizabeth Hoyt's first book, and a very popular book, too. My first read from Hoyt was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/156565.The_Leopard_Prince__Princes_Trilogy___2_' title='The Leopard Prince (Princes Trilogy, #2) by Elizabeth Hoyt' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Leopard Prince</a>, which came after this book. I was blown away by the way she tells a story, I still believe that she writes on a different level than a lot of the writers out there and is very talented.<br/><br/>But I didn't think this book was all that special. I disliked the heroine Anna intensely. I </span>
  <span id="freeText16004491165576575121" style="display:none">OK I am going to say something that is very unpopular here: I did not like this book. <br /><br />I believe that this book was Elizabeth Hoyt's first book, and a very popular book, too. My first read from Hoyt was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/156565.The_Leopard_Prince__Princes_Trilogy___2_" title="The Leopard Prince (Princes Trilogy, #2) by Elizabeth Hoyt" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Leopard Prince</a>, which came after this book. I was blown away by the way she tells a story, I still believe that she writes on a different level than a lot of the writers out there and is very talented.<br /><br />But I didn't think this book was all that special. I disliked the heroine Anna intensely. I don't understand why Edward felt compelled to marry her. The sex scenes are hot, yeah, but I skim-read them, in the beginning I was just disgusted then I was bored. <br /><br />This book, being such a wildly popular book, I will skip the summary. There must be great reviews out there that detail the plots. I will use my review to explain why I ended up skim-reading this book. <br /><br />I will start with what I liked. I liked that Edward was scarred by small pox and felt insecure about it. I liked that Coral saw through Anna's hypocrisy and called a spade a spade. I liked that Anna refused to marry Edward, even though it was a half-ass refusal (come on admit it, Anna, you WANTED TO marry him). I wanted to write one more what I liked, but I couldn't find anything else. So this is it. <br /><br />What I did not like (and I try to remain calm): <br /><br /><b>Anna Wren</b>, aka the chaste widow heroine: Anna Wren, from where I see it, is a HYPOCRITE. She was all hots for Edward, but could not bring herself to tell him. Then she lied to Edward, pretended to be a prostitute and had sex with Edward then she had the nerves to feel bad about it afterwards. Hoyt already touched on it herself in the book and put it rather poignantly: Anna was making love. Edward was just having sex. But Anna Wren, what did you think was going to happen? What were you expecting? Earth-shattering sex and love?? I have no word for this heroine. I simply despise her. <br /><br />I totally thought it refreshing that Anna wanted to JUST HAVE SEX LIKE A MAN. No problem. I admire that. Do it. But why lie about it? And worse: why feel ashamed about it? If she was going to feel ashamed about what she did, she should have never done it. That is rule number one: if you feel ashamed about something, you probably shouldn't do it. If you have already done it, then live with it. Don't sit there and feel bad and start wondering oh why is something missing. She asked for sex, she got sex. There was nothing missing in that sexual act. What was missing was her brain. <br /><br />I could go on and on about Anna, because I really did not like her. But I will just stop here before I say something really mean. I did not like her, personal opinion. If she was my friend I would have kicked her in the butt and told her to get a grip of herself. Do or not do, make a decision and live with it. Don't give me this crap about oh I wish he would let me kiss him when we had sex. What do you think is going on? He thought he was having sex with a prostitute and you made him believe that. <br /><br />(deep breath) <br /><br />But I did not like Anna, it became exceedingly difficult for me to like the story. I had an extremely unflattering picture for Anna, a rather plain-looking widow who was not honest with herself and the man she lusted after, but had the gulls to pretend to be a chaste widow. And of course she rather considered herself funny and brave. She was not afraid of Edward, that must spell courage. <br /><br />Oh how this woman annoyed me. The last time I was this annoyed with a heroine was when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6584134.Nine_Rules_to_Break_When_Romancing_a_Rake__Love_By_Numbers___1_" title="Nine Rules to Break When Romancing a Rake (Love By Numbers, #1) by Sarah MacLean" rel="nofollow noopener"> Nine Rules to Break When Romancing a Rake</a>. I don't want to give Hoyt a 1 star but that is hardly fair. Sarah Maclean got a 1 star from me for that pathetic heroine Callie. <br /><br />I will leave a 2 star rating for now. I would have liked to give this book at least 3 stars because I truly like Elizabeth Hoyt as a writer. But I am not certain I can do that after I examined my feelings toward Anna. I honestly would not mind if Anna was a real slut, whatever that word means. Make her horny, for Edward or for many other men, since she seemed so determined to have some great sex. It is alright. No judgements, seriously. But a woman who could not face herself and her lusts, who had to lie to extort sex, and could not live with herself for doing that, I have no respect for that. <br /><br />(deep breath)<br /><br />Namaste.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16004491165576575121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3069649805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3069649805" />
    <a title="Alp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26653561-alp"><img alt="Alp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462791280p2/26653561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3069649805?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alp" href="/user/show/26653561-alp">Alp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=tortured-hero">tortured-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=brooding-hero">brooding-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3069649805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5584736827824748990">Simply perfect. <br/>I loved this book--everything about it. If I could, I would give this one more than 5 stars!<br/></span>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3566710044242865700">Ah, more corset stuff. I REALLY liked this one though, the dialogue and characters were fun. Totally unbelievable plot twists at times, but whatever, if you go with it it's fun. I would sign up this author as a guilty pleasure in the future. Like I said in another review, I haven't listed a lot of these corset books I've read lately because most of them are snoozers. This one's writing was very enjoyable and good enough to note for those who want to read smutty corset romance.<br/> <br/>Also has some real</span>
  <span id="freeText3566710044242865700" style="display:none">Ah, more corset stuff. I REALLY liked this one though, the dialogue and characters were fun. Totally unbelievable plot twists at times, but whatever, if you go with it it's fun. I would sign up this author as a guilty pleasure in the future. Like I said in another review, I haven't listed a lot of these corset books I've read lately because most of them are snoozers. This one's writing was very enjoyable and good enough to note for those who want to read smutty corset romance.<br /> <br />Also has some realllllly naughty bits too, so be forewarned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3566710044242865700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10303305464917993596">4.5 - one little plot point (and no, not the device at the end-is it wrong I was really hoping for that?) was too distracting for me. While the writing was purposeful and tight (in other words, REALLY good), as well at funny at times, I also have the beautiful/artistic factor, and here for me, I didn't notice that to be a strength (maybe on a reread!).<br/><br/>So why a 4.5, Sam? <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[You have a plot distracting you (Chilly) needlessly nefarious side characters (Felicity)-one and the same really</span></span>
  <span id="freeText10303305464917993596" style="display:none">4.5 - one little plot point (and no, not the device at the end-is it wrong I was really hoping for that?) was too distracting for me. While the writing was purposeful and tight (in other words, REALLY good), as well at funny at times, I also have the beautiful/artistic factor, and here for me, I didn't notice that to be a strength (maybe on a reread!).<br /><br />So why a 4.5, Sam? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[You have a plot distracting you (Chilly) needlessly nefarious side characters (Felicity)-one and the same really-  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Um, the way the romance develops and who it develops between. It's the how, it's the why, it's the realistic and understandable barriers, and it's their choices in the end. It's the build between Anna and Edward, and of course his eventual undoing. <br /><br />The heartbreaking moment in the stable I didn't think I'd recover from--honestly, it's a little funny to me how the characters paralleled Noah &amp; Gavin <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34346381.Illegal_Contact__The_Barons___1_" title="Illegal Contact (The Barons, #1) by Santino Hassell" rel="nofollow noopener">Illegal Contact</a> a bit, which I just read. The grouchy one with a temper who barely anyone can get along with, and the assertive and compassionate opposite who can handle the person and understands their own self-worth and then ultimately a reason that keeps them apart which makes sense in their worlds, so much it hurts.<br /><br />I'd love to do a longer, more detailed review but I was up too late finishing this! What a great read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12389848254042051104"> <b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b>This was better than expected! I liked the characters and the overall storyline. I just didn’t care for the Felicity drama <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[She was someone that the h’s husband cheated on her with and she’s married to a wealthy man in their town.   <span id="freeText12389848254042051104" style="display:none"> <b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b>This was better than expected! I liked the characters and the overall storyline. I just didn’t care for the Felicity drama <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She was someone that the h’s husband cheated on her with and she’s married to a wealthy man in their town. Blackmail, secret children, yada, yada, yada 🙄 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The h didn’t seem to care all that much, so why should I?! The fact that we focus on her POV a few times bugged me. I loved the dog and the valet was hilarious! I really would’ve loved more time with experiencing their HEA though since the story ends (before the epilogue) with them finally officially together. <br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Anna and Edward’s story. Widowed Anna is having troubles financially and decides to get a job and finds one being a secretary to the local mysterious (and grumpy) earl. Edward has lost his family being the sole survivor to a smallpox outbreak when he was younger as well as his wife and baby in childbirth, so he has a lot to be grumpy about. What Edward doesn’t expect is that his new secretary will turn his world upside down. When Anna discovers that Edward uses a brothel to meet his manly needs, she decides that she needs her womanly needs met too and concocts a plan. There is some side character drama, some hot sexy times, and some sweet moments...and they get a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>Point Of View (POV):</b> This alternated between focusing on Anna and Edward in 3rd person narrative (with a few sections focusing on a side character).<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good. I never skimmed and I thought it flowed well.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> No, they take a while to develop stronger feelings.<br /><br /><b>H (Hero) rating:</b> 4 stars. Edward. I liked him. I liked his hard exterior and sweet insides.<br /><br /><b>h (heroine) rating:</b> 4 stars. Anna. I liked her. I appreciated how she pushed against the expected and did what made her happy and what was right.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low, no tissues needed<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They both push away and also pursue the relationship at times  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Hot. They have some hot tension, chemistry, and scenes -- but not so much it takes away from the story. Hotter than the usual HR!<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>OW (Other Woman)/OM (Other Man) drama:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> Not IMO but close <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[though the H slept with what he thought was an OW when he had feelings for the h and he was engaged to someone else (more of a business arrangement) &lt;\spoiler&gt;<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> I wouldn’t consider them together enough to call it a separation <br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Loss of loved ones (off page), h’s husband cheated on her (off page), and death of a spouse (off page) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This had pretty good closure in what I would call a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be <u>Safe</u> for most safety gang readers<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating (see above)<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have both the h and H pushing away<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have a separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse<br />- <b>Does </b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_450770217" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450770217" />
    <a title="Blodeuedd Finland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1962503-blodeuedd-finland"><img alt="Blodeuedd Finland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287391226p2/1962503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/450770217?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blodeuedd Finland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blodeuedd Finland" href="/user/show/1962503-blodeuedd-finland">Blodeuedd Finland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1962503-blodeuedd-finland?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer450770217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5447436364918545391">I was unsure about the grade but I am just gonna go all bitchy on this book. Truth be told, I sat there reading and nitpicking and never truly connected. Did it make me want to read more by this author...no. Would it make me pick up more books by her if I found them at the library, no, and that really means it should get a 2. Which is still of course an ok grade.<br/><br/>So many things irritated me with this book. The first time Anna sees and hears Edward she thinks of one thing..is that how his voice so</span>
  <span id="freeText5447436364918545391" style="display:none">I was unsure about the grade but I am just gonna go all bitchy on this book. Truth be told, I sat there reading and nitpicking and never truly connected. Did it make me want to read more by this author...no. Would it make me pick up more books by her if I found them at the library, no, and that really means it should get a 2. Which is still of course an ok grade.<br /><br />So many things irritated me with this book. The first time Anna sees and hears Edward she thinks of one thing..is that how his voice sounds when making love? Honestly? Wtf, someone needs to get laid and fast. I doubt a prim 18th century widow would think that.<br /><br />Then she becomes his secretary, again, wtf is this? She is a woman! Then she dines and rides with him. Oh girl, do not talk about that your reputation might take a hit, everyone, I mean everyone would already think you are his mistress. And if they are not then something is seriously wrong with that village.<br /><br />The sexual tension continues *yawns*. She is also not repulsed by his scars cos he is pretty on the inside or whatever. Really? I found him to be quite the ass in the beginning. Also how they sparred at once. No no, that is not proper etiquette. You are obviously a loose woman. Why he keeps thinking of you are a virtuous saint I do not know.<br /><br />To the brothels! Yes she finds a note and begins to think why men gets to smex around but women don't. Hello, because that is the era you live in. Do not go all modern on me or I will kick your ass. Anyway, what does our prim heroine do, yes she talks to a whore for 2 minutes and decides to go to a brothel and have sex with Edward. What? When did this happen? I am totally lost by this plot. WHY on earth would you do that? Just lift your skirts to him in the library and have at it. Yes he would not think you all prim and proper afterwards but at least you would get laid. Pretending to be someone else behind a mask at a brothel is something that does not go through my head. You also put yourself up to be raped by strangers, sold, killed, where is your head?<br /><br />Of course he later finds out, duh, so we could totally have been spared the stupid brothel story, oh and I must also mention that he has a magic penis. A very magical penis that cures every womb.<br /><br />Let's see, anything else I can snark at....I actually liked that she took pity on the prostitute, that I liked.<br /><br />Oh the villains. Do not even get me started, another stupid plot that made no sense. Someone making a big deal of nothing. I could have been spared that too, it was just embarrassing and I wanted to hide behind my book.<br /><br />Last, I am sure all these things could have been forgiven one way or another but at the end I realized that I suffered through the book and never connected. Why would I connect to the prim widow who just thinks about sex. Or the earl who goes on and on about how ugly he is and lusts after his secretary. An easy way to fix that, try to seduce her, if that fails, pay her off. I did not feel the chemistry, I did not get why she liked him, or he her, as she was so plain. But hey she was outspoken, he must like a challenge.<br /><br />I fear that yes I like HR, but HR does not like me back. I keep trying and I am sure everyone thinks I love HR to pieces, but I don't. It seldom impresses me. I enjoy it, it's a good genre, good escapism in it's silliness. But great, no, not that often. Really seldom really.<br /><br />Would I recommend it..no not really</span>
  <a data-text-id="5447436364918545391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/295776326?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne " href="/user/show/7179798-susanne">Susanne </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7179798-susanne?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295776326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15703911080666619135"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372564i/725896.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>Historical Romance - 3.5 stars!</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>With his hands at the back of his head, squeezing water from his hair, his muscles stood out in sharp relief. The sun glinted off his flexed arms and chest, and his black underarm hair curled damply. Rivulets of grimy water, mixed with blood from ewe, ran down his chest and arms. His low-slung breeches clung to his hips and thighs, delineating the bulge of his manhood. He looked quite pagan.</i>
</blockquote> I so wanted to love this book. I really did. But for some unknown rea</span>
  <span id="freeText15703911080666619135" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372564i/725896.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Historical Romance - 3.5 stars!</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>With his hands at the back of his head, squeezing water from his hair, his muscles stood out in sharp relief. The sun glinted off his flexed arms and chest, and his black underarm hair curled damply. Rivulets of grimy water, mixed with blood from ewe, ran down his chest and arms. His low-slung breeches clung to his hips and thighs, delineating the bulge of his manhood. He looked quite pagan.</i>
</blockquote> I so wanted to love this book. I really did. But for some unknown reason I did not click with the main characters.<br><br>It is a story about widow Anna Wren who is in desperate need for employment. The Earl of Swartingham has just frightened off his two most recent secretaries and he is in desperate need for another one. So Anna gets the position as the Earl's secretary. She is attracted to him despite his smallpox scars. He is attracted to her despite her boring looks. <b>And when she realizes that he is leaving for London to get her out of his head, she follows him to London and poses as a high-prized whore at a bawdy house.</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>"He might recognize me if we meet again." Anna pushed the kipper to one side of her plate. "It would be so unladylike to return a second night."<br><br>"Yes, I do see your problem," Coral murmured. "One night in a brothel is perfectly respectable, whilst two comes perilously close to being déclassé.</blockquote>
</i> I had one main problem with this book. <b>I couldn't fathom their attraction.</b> Both of them thinks rather badly of the other but can't resist the attraction. It felt like the author told me of the attraction, but I couldn't feel it from the writing. It might have had something to do with the introduction. <br><br>On the other hand, there were some good parts as well. I liked Ms Hoyt's descriptions of the landscape. <b>If only the romance had felt as real as the flowers.</b> <br><blockquote>
  <i>Daffodils dotted the tender grass beneath the trees. The branches above wore only a fuzz of new leaves, and the sunshine broke through with hardy impediment. Each yellow daffodil shone translucent and perfect, creating a fragile fairyland.</i>
</blockquote> <b>It was also novel and hot!</b> I really liked the new twist and their meeting at the brothel was way beyond your standard historical romance. The tiny romance subplot was very sweet. I will definitely try more of Ms Hoyt in the future!<br><br><b>Thank you Karen for reading it with me! &lt;3 &lt;3</b><br><br>Hero 2 ♥ Heroine 3 ♥ Romance 2 ♥ Humor 2 ♥ Hotness 4</span>
  <a data-text-id="15703911080666619135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9407349012915421080">I was kind of into this, even though everything about it is ridiculous. I liked Anna. And Edward was saveable. Probably. I'm not a fan of him seeking out a brothel for his frustration in wanting his secretary and feeling constrained by class difference from acting on it.   <span id="freeText9407349012915421080" style="display:none">I was kind of into this, even though everything about it is ridiculous. I liked Anna. And Edward was saveable. Probably. I'm not a fan of him seeking out a brothel for his frustration in wanting his secretary and feeling constrained by class difference from acting on it. And her seeking him out at this weird upscale sex grotto very nearly worked (which was enough to be going on with). But I couldn't stand the clown Felicity. I hated every PoV switch to show her scheming and I hated that she's such a horrible person who is nevertheless successful in everything. And when she so effortlessly penetrated the privacy of Anna and Edward I found my desire to continue die a horrible death. There was plenty of story in Anna and Edward all on their own. Intrusions by an awful person with unfounded enmity granted successes by authorial fiat gave me such a distaste of everything else that I just quit.</span>

<div id="review_3034946939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3034946939" />
    <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads"><img alt="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380942477p2/4197769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3034946939?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads">Jacqueline&#39;s Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9781455513581" href="/book/show/12687572-the-raven-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3034946939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5545066645824470224"><b>4 Stars</b><br/><br/>Elizabeth Hoyt has been on my TBR list for historical romance authors for sometime now. When I’m in a Historical Romance binge, I’m in it. I like to read series for days. Anyhow, I liked the Raven Prince. I did find it a bit wordy at times and a little too descriptive, but the overall story, angst, and characters were my jam.<br/><br/>It’s a meaty book and I did read it in two days.<br/><br/>The thing that got me was the storyline, although there was a part I wasn’t fond of, thankfully it wasn’t the FULL sto</span>
  <span id="freeText5545066645824470224" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br /><br />Elizabeth Hoyt has been on my TBR list for historical romance authors for sometime now. When I’m in a Historical Romance binge, I’m in it. I like to read series for days. Anyhow, I liked the Raven Prince. I did find it a bit wordy at times and a little too descriptive, but the overall story, angst, and characters were my jam.<br /><br />It’s a meaty book and I did read it in two days.<br /><br />The thing that got me was the storyline, although there was a part I wasn’t fond of, thankfully it wasn’t the FULL story and I can see how that would upset readers. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Earl gets engaged while he pursues Anna, yeah wasn’t happy about that <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The Earl is the typical Hero. He has scars on his face and he doesn’t do “society”. He needs a secretary ASAP.<br /><br />Anna is a Widow and she’s in need of money. She’s a lady and shouldn’t work, but she doesn’t want to starve and so she becomes the Earl’s secretary.<br /><br />What I liked most about the book was the Earl’s attraction towards Anna. I like it when the Hero chases after the Heroine. But the Earl needs a wife because he needs children and the thing is, Anna doesn’t have any children and that’s after 4 years of marriage to her late husband. <br /><br />Oh the problems.<br /><br />I didn’t care for the “problems” in the book, I just liked reading about The Earl chasing after Anna. I liked that Anna was strong and she was a good person. I liked that she put the Earl in his place and she made the book enjoyable for me.<br /><br />Overall, a great start to the series. I’m not sure if I will continue since the reviews for the rest of the series is dicey. I might start a different series and just follow the reviews. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5545066645824470224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SISZvVFRqihF/e2BSQgssVQw4dcbJPu5+wgSuqHlA9imYGa850XhlDw2AbixeC27okvcp6mC9NsSiXwNA6Y11g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

She also writes deliciously fun contemporary romance under the name Julia Harper. Elizabeth lives in Minneapolis, Minnesota with three untrained dogs and one long-suffering husband.<br/></span>
